[BWV 1081–1126](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_compositions_by_Johann_Sebastian_Bach#20th-century_additions_to_the_BWV_catalogue_and_Anhang "List of compositions by Johann Sebastian Bach") were added to the catalogue in the second half of the 20th century, and [BWV 1127 and higher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_compositions_by_Johann_Sebastian_Bach#BWV_Later "List of compositions by Johann Sebastian Bach") are 21st-century additions.<sup id="cite_ref-137"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BDW1307_138-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-BDW1307-138">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kuznik2008_139-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Kuznik2008-139">[137]</a></sup>

### Passions and oratorios

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Lama_asabthani.tif/lossy-page1-300px-Lama_asabthani.tif.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lama_asabthani.tif)

Bach's autograph of the recitative with the gospel text of Christ's death from _St Matthew Passion_ ([Matthew 27:45–47a](https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Bible_(Wikisource)/Matthew#27:45 "s:Bible (Wikisource)/Matthew"))

Bach composed [Passions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Passions_(Bach) "Passions (Bach)") for Good Friday services and oratorios such as the _[Christmas Oratorio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christmas_Oratorio "Christmas Oratorio")_, which is a set of six cantatas for use in the [liturgical season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liturgical_year "Liturgical year") of Christmas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELeaver2007430_140-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTELeaver2007430-140">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2003a114_141-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2003a114-141">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup> Shorter oratorios include the _[Easter Oratorio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Easter_Oratorio "Easter Oratorio")_ and the _[Ascension Oratorio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lobet_Gott_in_seinen_Reichen,_BWV_11 "Lobet Gott in seinen Reichen, BWV 11")_. With its double choir and orchestra, the _[St Matthew Passion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St_Matthew_Passion "St Matthew Passion")_ is one of Bach's most extended works. The _[St John Passion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St_John_Passion "St John Passion")_ was the first passion Bach composed during his tenure as Thomaskantor in Leipzig.

### Cantatas

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bach_-_cantata_140._1._chorus.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 5 minutes and 48 seconds.

---

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bach_-_cantata_140._2._recitative.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 1 minute and 8 seconds.

---

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bach_-_cantata_140._3._duet.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 5 minutes and 56 seconds.

---

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bach_-_cantata_140._4._chorale.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 4 minutes and 41 seconds.

---

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bach_-_cantata_140._5._recitative.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 1 minute and 6 seconds.

---

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bach_-_cantata_140._6._duet.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 5 minutes and 41 seconds.

---

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bach_-_cantata_140._7._chorale.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 1 minute and 39 seconds.

According to his obituary, Bach would have composed [five year-cycles of sacred cantatas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach%27s_cantata_cycles "Bach's cantata cycles"), and additional church cantatas for weddings and funerals, for example.<sup id="cite_ref-Nekrolog_94-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Nekrolog-94">[92]</a></sup> Approximately 200 of these sacred works are extant, an estimated two thirds of the total number of church cantatas he composed.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolff5_65-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Wolff5-65">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> The [Bach Digital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach_Digital "Bach Digital") website lists 50 known secular cantatas by the composer,<sup id="cite_ref-BDWlist_144-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-BDWlist-144">[142]</a></sup> about half of which are extant or largely reconstructable.<sup id="cite_ref-145"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup>

#### Church cantatas

Bach's cantatas vary greatly in form and instrumentation. Many consist of a large opening chorus followed by one or more recitative-aria pairs for soloists (or duets) and a concluding chorale. The melody of the concluding chorale often appears as a [cantus firmus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cantus_firmus "Cantus firmus") in the opening movement.<sup id="cite_ref-146"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup>

[Bach's earliest cantatas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach%27s_early_cantatas "Bach's early cantatas") date from his years in Arnstadt and Mühlhausen. The earliest surviving work in the genre is [_Nach dir, Herr, verlanget mich_, BWV 150](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nach_dir,_Herr,_verlanget_mich,_BWV_150 "Nach dir, Herr, verlanget mich, BWV 150"). As a whole, the extant early works all show remarkable mastery and skill. Many feature an instrumental opening which display effective use of the limited instrumental forces available to Bach, whether it be in the subdued combination of two recorders and two viola de gamba for [BWV 106](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gottes_Zeit_ist_die_allerbeste_Zeit,_BWV_106 "Gottes Zeit ist die allerbeste Zeit, BWV 106"), or the independent bassoon in [BWV 196](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Der_Herr_denket_an_uns,_BWV_196 "Der Herr denket an uns, BWV 196"). Bach's compositional skills are also manifested through his daring harmonies and advanced, unprecedented chord progressions. According to [Christoph Wolff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christoph_Wolff "Christoph Wolff"), Bach's early cantatas are impressive evidence of how the modest means at his disposal did not restrain the composer in the slightest, and they compare favourably with compositions by the most talented composers from the beginning of the 18th century, such as [Krieger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Philipp_Krieger "Johann Philipp Krieger"), [Kuhnau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Kuhnau "Johann Kuhnau") or [Zachow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Wilhelm_Zachow "Friedrich Wilhelm Zachow").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWolff2000100–101_147-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolff2000100%E2%80%93101-147">[145]</a></sup>

After taking up his office as _[Thomaskantor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomaskantor "Thomaskantor")_ in late May 1723, Bach performed a cantata each Sunday and feast day, corresponding to the [lectionary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lectionary "Lectionary") readings of the week.<sup id="cite_ref-Baroquenet_24-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Baroquenet-24">[22]</a></sup> [His first cantata cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach%27s_first_cantata_cycle "Bach's first cantata cycle") ran from the first Sunday after [Trinity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trinity_Sunday "Trinity Sunday") of 1723 to Trinity Sunday the next year. For instance, the Visitation cantata [_Herz und Mund und Tat und Leben_, BWV 147](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herz_und_Mund_und_Tat_und_Leben,_BWV_147 "Herz und Mund und Tat und Leben, BWV 147"), containing the chorale that is known in English as "Jesu, Joy of Man's Desiring", belongs to this first cycle. The cantata cycle of his second year in Leipzig is called the [chorale cantata cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chorale_cantata_cycle "Chorale cantata cycle") as it consists mainly of works in the [chorale cantata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chorale_cantata "Chorale cantata") format. [His third cantata cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach%27s_third_cantata_cycle "Bach's third cantata cycle") was developed over a period of several years, followed by the [Picander cycle of 1728–29](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Picander_cycle_of_1728%E2%80%9329 "Picander cycle of 1728–29").

Later church cantatas include the chorale cantatas [_Ein feste Burg ist unser Gott_, BWV 80](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ein_feste_Burg_ist_unser_Gott,_BWV_80 "Ein feste Burg ist unser Gott, BWV 80") (final version)<sup id="cite_ref-148"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> and [_Wachet auf, ruft uns die Stimme_, BWV 140](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wachet_auf,_ruft_uns_die_Stimme,_BWV_140 "Wachet auf, ruft uns die Stimme, BWV 140").<sup id="cite_ref-149"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> Only the first three Leipzig cycles are more or less completely extant. Apart from his own work, Bach also performed cantatas by Telemann and by his distant relative [Johann Ludwig Bach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Ludwig_Bach "Johann Ludwig Bach").<sup id="cite_ref-Baroquenet_24-6"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Baroquenet-24">[22]</a></sup>

#### Secular cantatas

Bach also wrote secular cantatas, for instance for members of the royal Polish and prince-electoral Saxonian families (e.g. _[Trauer-Ode](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trauer-Ode "Trauer-Ode")_),<sup id="cite_ref-150"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup> or other public or private occasions (e.g. _[Hunting Cantata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunting_Cantata "Hunting Cantata")_).<sup id="cite_ref-151"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup> The text of these cantatas was occasionally in dialect (e.g. _[Peasant Cantata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peasant_Cantata "Peasant Cantata")_)<sup id="cite_ref-152"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup> or Italian (e.g. _[Amore traditore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amore_traditore "Amore traditore")_).<sup id="cite_ref-153"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> Many of the secular cantatas were lost, but for some of them the text and occasion are known, for instance when Picander later published their librettos (e.g. [BWV Anh. 11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BWV_Anh._11 "BWV Anh. 11")–[12](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BWV_Anh._12 "BWV Anh. 12")).<sup id="cite_ref-154"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup>

Some of the surviving secular cantatas have a plot involving mythological figures of Greek antiquity (e.g. _[Der Streit zwischen Phoebus und Pan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Der_Streit_zwischen_Phoebus_und_Pan "Der Streit zwischen Phoebus und Pan")_),<sup id="cite_ref-155"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> and others were almost miniature [_buffo_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opera_buffa "Opera buffa") operas (e.g. _[Coffee Cantata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coffee_Cantata "Coffee Cantata")_).<sup id="cite_ref-156"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> Although Bach never expressed any interest in opera,<sup id="cite_ref-157"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup> his secular cantatas, or _[drammi per musica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dramma_per_musica "Dramma per musica")_, would have allowed Leipzig audiences, deprived of opera since 1720, to experience musical performances comparable to the royal opera in Dresden. These were not at all "poor or makeshift substitutes for real opera" but spectacles displaying "full mastery of the dramatic genre and the proper pacing of the dialogues."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWolff2000363_158-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolff2000363-158">[156]</a></sup>

### A cappella music

Bach's a cappella music includes motets and chorale harmonisations.

#### Motets

Bach's [motets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_motets_by_Johann_Sebastian_Bach "List of motets by Johann Sebastian Bach") (BWV 225–231) are pieces on sacred themes for choir and continuo, with instruments playing [colla parte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colla_parte "Colla parte"). Several of them were composed for funerals.<sup id="cite_ref-159"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> The six motets definitely composed by Bach are _[Singet dem Herrn ein neues Lied](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Singet_dem_Herrn_ein_neues_Lied,_BWV_225 "Singet dem Herrn ein neues Lied, BWV 225")_, _[Der Geist hilft unser Schwachheit auf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Der_Geist_hilft_unser_Schwachheit_auf,_BWV_226 "Der Geist hilft unser Schwachheit auf, BWV 226")_, _[Jesu, meine Freude](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesu,_meine_Freude,_BWV_227 "Jesu, meine Freude, BWV 227")_, _[Fürchte dich nicht](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/F%C3%BCrchte_dich_nicht,_BWV_228 "Fürchte dich nicht, BWV 228")_, _[Komm, Jesu, komm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Komm,_Jesu,_komm,_BWV_229 "Komm, Jesu, komm, BWV 229")_, and _[Lobet den Herrn, alle Heiden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lobet_den_Herrn,_alle_Heiden,_BWV_230 "Lobet den Herrn, alle Heiden, BWV 230")_. The motet _Sei Lob und Preis mit Ehren_ (BWV 231) is part of the composite motet _[Jauchzet dem Herrn, alle Welt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jauchzet_dem_Herrn,_alle_Welt,_BWV_Anh_160 "Jauchzet dem Herrn, alle Welt, BWV Anh 160")_ ([BWV Anh.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BWV_Anh. "BWV Anh.") 160), other parts of which may be based on work by Telemann.<sup id="cite_ref-160"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup>

#### Chorale harmonisations

Bach wrote hundreds of four-part harmonisations of Lutheran chorales.

### Church music in Latin

Bach's church music in Latin includes the [Magnificat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnificat_(Bach) "Magnificat (Bach)"), four [Kyrie–Gloria Masses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Missa_(Bach) "Missa (Bach)"), and the [Mass in B minor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_in_B_minor "Mass in B minor").

#### Magnificat

The [first version of Bach's Magnificat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnificat_in_E-flat_major,_BWV_243a "Magnificat in E-flat major, BWV 243a") dates from 1723, but the work is best known in its [D major version](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnificat_in_D_major,_BWV_243 "Magnificat in D major, BWV 243") of 1733.

#### Mass in B minor

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Johann_Sebastian_Bach_-_Mass_in_B_minor_-_Agnus_Dei.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 4 minutes and 41 seconds.

performed by Solomija Drozd (voice), Petro Titiajev (violin) and Ivan Ostapovych (organ)

In 1733 Bach composed a [Kyrie–Gloria Mass for the Dresden court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_for_the_Dresden_court_(Bach) "Mass for the Dresden court (Bach)"). Near the end of his life, around 1748–1749, he expanded this composition into the large-scale [Mass in B minor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_in_B_minor "Mass in B minor"). The work was never performed in full during Bach's lifetime.<sup id="cite_ref-161"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerz1985187_162-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerz1985187-162">[160]</a></sup>

### Keyboard music

Bach wrote for organ and for [stringed keyboard instruments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stringed_keyboard_instrument "Stringed keyboard instrument") such as [harpsichord](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harpsichord "Harpsichord"), [clavichord](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clavichord "Clavichord") and [lute-harpsichord](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lute-harpsichord "Lute-harpsichord").

#### Organ works

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Johann_Sebastian_Bach_Prelude_in_A_minor_BWV_543_Robert_K%C3%B6bler_Silbermann-Organ.mp3 "Play audio")Duration: 3 minutes and 18 seconds.

---

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Johann_Sebastian_Bach_Fugue_in_A_minor_BWV_543_Robert_K%C3%B6bler_Silbermann-Organ.mp3 "Play audio")Duration: 6 minutes and 25 seconds.

Bach was best known during his lifetime as an organist, organ consultant, and composer of organ works in both the traditional German free genres (such as [preludes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prelude_(music) "Prelude (music)"), [fantasias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fantasia_(music) "Fantasia (music)"), and [toccatas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toccata "Toccata")) and stricter forms (such as [chorale preludes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chorale_prelude "Chorale prelude") and fugues).<sup id="cite_ref-Baroquenet_24-7"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Baroquenet-24">[22]</a></sup> At a young age, he established a reputation for creativity and ability to integrate foreign styles into his organ works. A decidedly North German influence was exerted by [Georg Böhm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georg_B%C3%B6hm "Georg Böhm"), with whom Bach came into contact in Lüneburg, and [Dieterich Buxtehude](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dieterich_Buxtehude "Dieterich Buxtehude"), whom the young organist visited in Lübeck in 1704 on an extended leave of absence from his job in Arnstadt. Around this time, Bach copied the works of numerous French and Italian composers to gain insights into their compositional languages, and later arranged violin concertos by Vivaldi and others for organ and harpsichord. During his most productive period (1708–1714) he composed about a dozen pairs of preludes and fugues, five toccatas and fugues, and the _[Orgelbüchlein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orgelb%C3%BCchlein "Orgelbüchlein")_ or "Little Organ Book", an unfinished collection of 46 short chorale preludes that demonstrate compositional techniques in the setting of chorale tunes. After leaving Weimar, Bach wrote less for organ, although some of his best-known works (the six [Organ Sonatas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organ_Sonatas_(Bach) "Organ Sonatas (Bach)"), the German Organ Mass in [_Clavier-Übung_ III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clavier-%C3%9Cbung_III "Clavier-Übung III") from 1739, and the [Great Eighteen Chorale Preludes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Eighteen_Chorale_Preludes "Great Eighteen Chorale Preludes"), revised late in his life) were composed after leaving Weimar. Bach was extensively engaged later in his life in consulting on organ projects, testing new organs and dedicating organs in afternoon recitals.<sup id="cite_ref-163"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup> The [Canonic Variations on "Vom Himmel hoch da komm' ich her"](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canonic_Variations_on_%22Vom_Himmel_hoch_da_komm%27_ich_her%22 "Canonic Variations on "Vom Himmel hoch da komm' ich her"") and the _[Schübler Chorales](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sch%C3%BCbler_Chorales "Schübler Chorales")_ are organ works Bach published in the last years of his life.

#### Harpsichord and other stringed keyboard instruments

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Title_page_of_The_Art_of_Fugue.jpg/220px-Title_page_of_The_Art_of_Fugue.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Title_page_of_The_Art_of_Fugue.jpg)

_The Art of Fugue_ (title page) – performed by Mehmet Okonsar on organ and harpsichord

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ArtofFugue-Part1of2-1to12.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 39 minutes and 53 seconds.[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ArtofFugue-Part1of2-1to12.ogg)

Nos. 1–12

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ArtofFugue-Part2of2-13to20.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 31 minutes and 2 seconds.[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:ArtofFugue-Part2of2-13to20.ogg)

Nos. 13–20

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bach_C_Major_Prelude_Werckmeister.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 1 minute and 58 seconds.

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Johann_Sebastian_Bach_-_Italian_Concerto_-_F_Major_-_1st_movement.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 4 minutes and 24 seconds.

---

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Johann_Sebastian_Bach_-_Italian_Concerto_-_F_Major_-_Andante.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 5 minutes and 30 seconds.

---

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Johann_Sebastian_Bach_-_Italian_Concerto_-_F_Major_-_Presto.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 3 minutes and 17 seconds.

Bach wrote many works for harpsichord, some of which may also have been played on the clavichord or lute-harpsichord. Some of his larger works, such as [_Clavier-Übung_ II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clavier-%C3%9Cbung_II "Clavier-Übung II") and [IV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clavier-%C3%9Cbung_IV "Clavier-Übung IV"), are intended for a harpsichord with two manuals: performing them on a keyboard instrument with a single manual (like a piano) may present technical difficulties for the crossing of hands.

-   _[The Well-Tempered Clavier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Well-Tempered_Clavier "The Well-Tempered Clavier")_, Books 1 and 2 (BWV 846–893). Each book consists of a prelude and fugue in each of the 24 major and minor [keys](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Key_(music) "Key (music)"), in chromatic order from C major to B minor (thus, the whole collection is often referred to as "the 48"). "Well-tempered" in the title refers to the [temperament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Musical_temperament "Musical temperament") (system of tuning); many temperaments before Bach's time were not flexible enough to allow compositions to utilise more than just a few keys.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchweitzer1923333_165-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchweitzer1923333-165">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup>
-   The _[Inventions and Sinfonias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inventions_and_Sinfonias_(Bach) "Inventions and Sinfonias (Bach)")_ (BWV 772–801). These short two- and three-part contrapuntal works are arranged in the same chromatic order as _The Well-Tempered Clavier_, omitting some of the rarer keys. These pieces were intended by Bach for instructional purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-167"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup>
-   Three collections of [dance suites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suite_(music) "Suite (music)"): the _[English Suites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_Suites_(Bach) "English Suites (Bach)")_ (BWV 806–811), _[French Suites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Suites_(Bach) "French Suites (Bach)")_ (BWV 812–817), and [Partitas for keyboard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partitas_for_keyboard_(Bach) "Partitas for keyboard (Bach)") (_Clavier-Übung I_, BWV 825–830). Each collection contains six suites built on the standard model (_[allemande](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allemande "Allemande")_–_[courante](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Courante "Courante")_–_[sarabande](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarabande "Sarabande")_–(optional movement)–_[gigue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gigue "Gigue")_). The English Suites closely follow the traditional model, adding a prelude before the _allemande_ and including a single movement between the _sarabande_ and _gigue_.<sup id="cite_ref-168"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> The French Suites omit preludes but have multiple movements between the _sarabande_ and _gigue_.<sup id="cite_ref-169"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup> The partitas expand the model further with elaborate introductory movements and miscellaneous movements between the basic elements of the model.<sup id="cite_ref-170"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup>
-   The _[Goldberg Variations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goldberg_Variations "Goldberg Variations")_ (BWV 988), an aria with 30 [variations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variation_(music) "Variation (music)"). The collection has a complex and unconventional structure: the variations build on the [bass line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bassline "Bassline") of the aria rather than its melody, and musical [canons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canon_(music) "Canon (music)") are interpolated according to a grand plan. There are 9 canons within the 30 variations; every third variation is a canon.<sup id="cite_ref-171"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> These variations move in order from canon at unison to canon at the ninth. The first eight are in pairs (unison and octave, second and seventh, third and sixth, fourth and fifth). The ninth canon stands on its own due to compositional dissimilarities. The final variation, instead of being the expected canon at the tenth, is a [quodlibet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quodlibet "Quodlibet").
-   Miscellaneous pieces such as the _[Overture in the French Style](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overture_in_the_French_style,_BWV_831 "Overture in the French style, BWV 831")_ (_French Overture_, BWV 831) and the _[Italian Concerto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Concerto_(Bach) "Italian Concerto (Bach)")_ (BWV 971) (published together as _Clavier-Übung II_), and the _[Chromatic Fantasia and Fugue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromatic_Fantasia_and_Fugue "Chromatic Fantasia and Fugue")_ (BWV 903).

Among Bach's lesser known keyboard works are seven [toccatas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toccata "Toccata") [(BWV 910–916)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toccatas_for_Keyboard_(Bach) "Toccatas for Keyboard (Bach)"), [four duets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duets_(Bach) "Duets (Bach)") (BWV 802–805), [sonatas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sonata "Sonata") for keyboard (BWV 963–967), the [Six Little Preludes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six_Little_Preludes_(Bach) "Six Little Preludes (Bach)") (BWV 933–938), and the _[Aria variata alla maniera italiana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aria_variata_alla_maniera_italiana "Aria variata alla maniera italiana")_ (BWV 989).

### Orchestral and chamber music

Bach wrote for single instruments, duets, and small ensembles. Many of his solo works, such as the six [sonatas and partitas for violin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sonatas_and_Partitas_for_Solo_Violin_(Bach) "Sonatas and Partitas for Solo Violin (Bach)") (BWV 1001–1006) and the six [cello suites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cello_Suites_(Bach) "Cello Suites (Bach)") (BWV 1007–1012), are widely considered to be among the most profound in the repertoire.<sup id="cite_ref-172"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lester_127-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Lester-127">[125]</a></sup> He wrote sonatas for a solo instrument such as the viola de gamba accompanied by harpsichord or continuo, as well as trio sonatas (two instruments and continuo).

_The Musical Offering_ and _The Art of Fugue_ are late contrapuntal works containing pieces for unspecified instruments or combinations of instruments.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWolff1991111_173-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolff1991111-173">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup>

#### Violin concertos

Surviving works in the concerto form include two violin concertos ([BWV 1041](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Violin_Concerto_in_A_minor_(Bach) "Violin Concerto in A minor (Bach)") in A minor and [BWV 1042](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Violin_Concerto_in_E_major_(Bach) "Violin Concerto in E major (Bach)") in E major) and a concerto for two violins in D minor, [BWV 1043](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concerto_for_Two_Violins_(Bach) "Concerto for Two Violins (Bach)"), often referred to as Bach's "double concerto".

#### _Brandenburg Concertos_

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Brandenburg_Concerto_No._4_in_G,_Movement_I_(Allegro),_BWV_1049_(ISRC_USUAN1100303).oga "Play audio")Duration: 7 minutes and 18 seconds.

---

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bach_-_Brandenburg_ConcertoNo._4_in_G_Major-_II._Andante.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 4 minutes and 36 seconds.

---

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bach_-_Brandenburg_Concerto.No.4_in_G_Major-_III._Presto.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 4 minutes and 17 seconds.

Bach's best-known orchestral works are the _Brandenburg Concertos_, so named because he submitted them in the hope of gaining employment from [Margrave Christian Ludwig of Brandenburg-Schwedt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margrave_Christian_Ludwig_of_Brandenburg-Schwedt "Margrave Christian Ludwig of Brandenburg-Schwedt") in 1721; his application was unsuccessful.<sup id="cite_ref-Baroquenet_24-8"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Baroquenet-24">[22]</a></sup> These works are examples of the [concerto grosso](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concerto_grosso "Concerto grosso") genre.

#### Keyboard concertos

Bach composed and transcribed concertos for one to four harpsichords. Many of the harpsichord concertos were not original works but arrangements of his concertos for other instruments, now lost.<sup id="cite_ref-175"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup> A number of violin, oboe, and flute concertos have been reconstructed from these.

#### Orchestral suites

In addition to concertos, Bach wrote four [orchestral suites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orchestral_suites_(Bach) "Orchestral suites (Bach)"), each suite being a series of stylised dances for orchestra, preceded by a [French overture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_overture "French overture").<sup id="cite_ref-176"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup>

### Copies, arrangements and uncertain attributions

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wiki_naxos_8.550194_01_13.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 2 minutes and 50 seconds.

---

[](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sheep_May_Safely_Graze_BWV_208.ogg "Play audio")Duration: 3 minutes and 58 seconds.

The aria "Schafe können sicher weiden" (Sheep May Safely Graze), No. 9 from the _[Hunting Cantata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunting_Cantata "Hunting Cantata")_, BWV 208: composed for soprano, recorders, and continuo, the music of this movement exists in a variety of instrumental arrangements.

In his early youth, Bach copied pieces by other composers to learn from them.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen49mode2up_10–11]_177-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen49mode2up_10%E2%80%9311]-177">[175]</a></sup> Later, he copied and arranged music for performance or as study material for his pupils. Some of these pieces, like "[Bist du bei mir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bist_du_bei_mir "Bist du bei mir")" (copied not by Bach but by Anna Magdalena), became famous before being dissociated with Bach. Bach copied and arranged Italian masters such as Vivaldi (e.g. [BWV 1065](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BWV_1065 "BWV 1065")), [Pergolesi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Pergolesi "Giovanni Battista Pergolesi") ([BWV 1083](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BWV_1083 "BWV 1083")) and [Palestrina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giovanni_Pierluigi_da_Palestrina "Giovanni Pierluigi da Palestrina") ([Missa Sine nomine](https://imslp.org/wiki/Missa_Sine_nomine_(Palestrina,_Giovanni_Pierluigi_da)#Arrangements_and_Transcriptions "scores:Missa Sine nomine (Palestrina, Giovanni Pierluigi da)")), French masters such as [François Couperin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Couperin "François Couperin") ([BWV Anh. 183](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Notebook_for_Anna_Magdalena_Bach#The_1725_notebook "Notebook for Anna Magdalena Bach")), and, closer to home, various German masters including Telemann (e.g. [BWV 824](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_solo_keyboard_compositions_by_Johann_Sebastian_Bach#Miscellaneous_suites_(818%E2%80%93824) "List of solo keyboard compositions by Johann Sebastian Bach")\=[TWV 32:14](https://imslp.org/wiki/Suite_in_A_major,_TWV_32:14_(Telemann,_Georg_Philipp) "scores:Suite in A major, TWV 32:14 (Telemann, Georg Philipp)")) and Handel ([arias from _Brockes Passion_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St_Mark_Passion_pastiche#Leipzig_1747%E2%80%931748_(BC_D_5) "St Mark Passion pastiche")), and music from members of his own family. He also often copied and arranged his own music (e.g. movements from cantatas for his short masses [BWV 233–236](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyrie%E2%80%93Gloria_masses,_BWV_233%E2%80%93236 "Kyrie–Gloria masses, BWV 233–236")), as his music was likewise copied and arranged by others. Some of these arrangements, like the late 19th-century "[Air on the G String](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_on_the_G_String "Air on the G String")", helped to popularise Bach's music.

Sometimes "who copied whom" is not clear. For instance, Forkel mentions a Mass for double chorus among the works composed by Bach. The work was published and performed in the early 19th century, and although a score partially in Bach's handwriting exists, the work was later considered spurious.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen187mode2up_140–141]_178-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen187mode2up_140%E2%80%93141]-178">[176]</a></sup> In 1950, the design of the Bach-Werke-Verzeichnis was to keep such works out of the main catalogue: if there was a strong association with Bach they could be listed in its appendix (German: _Anhang_, abbreviated as Anh.). Thus, for instance, the aforementioned Mass for double chorus became [BWV Anh. 167](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach%27s_church_music_in_Latin#Copies "Bach's church music in Latin"). But this was far from the end of the attribution issues. For instance, [_Schlage doch, gewünschte Stunde_, BWV 53](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schlage_doch,_gew%C3%BCnschte_Stunde,_BWV_53 "Schlage doch, gewünschte Stunde, BWV 53"), was later attributed to [Melchior Hoffmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melchior_Hoffmann_(composer) "Melchior Hoffmann (composer)"). For other works, Bach's authorship was put in doubt without a generally accepted answer to the question of whether or not he composed it: the best known organ composition in the BWV catalogue, the [Toccata and Fugue in D minor, BWV 565](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toccata_and_Fugue_in_D_minor,_BWV_565 "Toccata and Fugue in D minor, BWV 565"), was indicated as one of these uncertain works in the late 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-179"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup>

## Reception

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Arnstadt_Bachkirche_au%C3%9Fen_Chor_03.jpg/220px-Arnstadt_Bachkirche_au%C3%9Fen_Chor_03.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Arnstadt_Bachkirche_au%C3%9Fen_Chor_03.jpg)

The church in Arnstadt where Bach had been the organist from 1703 to 1707. In 1935 the church was renamed "Bachkirche".

Throughout the 18th century, the appreciation of Bach's music was mostly limited to distinguished connoisseurs. The 19th century started with publication of the first biography of the composer and ended with the completion of the publication of all of Bach's known works by the [Bach Gesellschaft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach_Gesellschaft "Bach Gesellschaft"). Starting with the [Bach Revival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach_Revival "Bach Revival"), he began to be regarded as one of the greatest composers, a reputation he has maintained ever since. The [BACH motif](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BACH_motif "BACH motif"), used by the composer in his own compositions, was used in dozens of tributes to the composer from the 19th century to the 21st.

### 18th century

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/17b_Bach-Bild_von_%27Gebel%27%2C_vor_1798.jpg/220px-17b_Bach-Bild_von_%27Gebel%27%2C_vor_1798.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:17b_Bach-Bild_von_%27Gebel%27,_vor_1798.jpg)

Painting of Johann Sebastian Bach by 'Gebel', before 1798

In his own time, Bach was highly regarded amongst his colleagues,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeck2003[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidN1zSVDYTCXgCpgPA141_141]_180-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeck2003[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidN1zSVDYTCXgCpgPA141_141]-180">[178]</a></sup> although his reputation outside of this small circle of connoisseurs was due not to his compositions (which had an extremely narrow circulation),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWolffEmery2001_12-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolffEmery2001-12">[11]</a></sup> but due to his virtuosic abilities. Nevertheless, during his life, Bach received public recognition, such as the title of court composer by [Augustus III of Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augustus_III_of_Poland "Augustus III of Poland") and the appreciation he was shown by [Frederick the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_the_Great "Frederick the Great") and [Hermann Karl von Keyserling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermann_Karl_von_Keyserling "Hermann Karl von Keyserling"). Such highly placed appreciation contrasted with the humiliations he had to cope with, for instance in Leipzig.<sup id="cite_ref-181"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup> Also in the contemporary press, Bach had his detractors, such as [Johann Adolf Scheibe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Adolf_Scheibe "Johann Adolf Scheibe"), suggesting he write less complex music, and his supporters, such as [Johann Mattheson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Mattheson "Johann Mattheson") and [Lorenz Christoph Mizler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lorenz_Christoph_Mizler "Lorenz Christoph Mizler").<sup id="cite_ref-182"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup>

After his death, Bach's reputation as a composer initially declined: his work was regarded as old-fashioned compared to the emerging [galant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galant_music "Galant music") style.<sup id="cite_ref-185"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup> He was remembered more as a virtuoso player of the organ and as a teacher. The bulk of the music that had been [printed during the composer's lifetime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_compositions_by_Johann_Sebastian_Bach_printed_during_his_lifetime "List of compositions by Johann Sebastian Bach printed during his lifetime"), at least the part that was remembered, was for the organ and the harpsichord. Thus, his reputation as a composer was initially mostly limited to his keyboard music, and that even fairly limited to its value in music education.

Bach's surviving family members, who inherited a large part of his manuscripts, were not all equally concerned with preserving them, leading to considerable losses.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWolff2000456–461_186-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolff2000456%E2%80%93461-186">[184]</a></sup> [Carl Philipp Emanuel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Philipp_Emanuel_Bach "Carl Philipp Emanuel Bach"), his second eldest son, was most active in safeguarding his father's legacy: he co-authored his father's obituary, contributed to the publication of his four-part chorales,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen130mode1up_85–86]_187-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen130mode1up_85%E2%80%9386]-187">[185]</a></sup> staged some of his works, and the bulk of previously unpublished works of his father were preserved with his help.<sup id="cite_ref-188"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup> [Wilhelm Friedemann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_Friedemann_Bach "Wilhelm Friedemann Bach"), the eldest son, performed several of his father's cantatas in [Halle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halle_(Saale) "Halle (Saale)") but after becoming unemployed sold part of the large collection of his father's works he owned.<sup id="cite_ref-189"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen186mode1up_139]_190-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen186mode1up_139]-190">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWolff2013459_191-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolff2013459-191">[189]</a></sup> Several [students of the old master](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_students_of_Johann_Sebastian_Bach "List of students of Johann Sebastian Bach"), such as his son-in-law [Johann Christoph Altnickol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Christoph_Altnickol "Johann Christoph Altnickol"), [Johann Friedrich Agricola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Friedrich_Agricola "Johann Friedrich Agricola"), [Johann Kirnberger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Kirnberger "Johann Kirnberger"), and [Johann Ludwig Krebs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Ludwig_Krebs "Johann Ludwig Krebs"), contributed to the dissemination of his legacy. The early devotees were not all musicians; for example, in Berlin, [Daniel Itzig](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daniel_Itzig "Daniel Itzig"), a high official of Frederick the Great's court, venerated Bach.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolff2005_192-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Wolff2005-192">[190]</a></sup> His eldest daughters took lessons from Kirnberger and their sister Sara from [Wilhelm Friedemann Bach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_Friedemann_Bach "Wilhelm Friedemann Bach"), who was in Berlin from 1774 to 1784.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolff2005_192-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Wolff2005-192">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Apple14_193-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Apple14-193">[191]</a></sup> Sara Itzig Levy became an avid collector of works by Johann Sebastian Bach and his sons and was a "patron" of CPE Bach.<sup id="cite_ref-Apple14_193-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Apple14-193">[191]</a></sup>

While in Leipzig, performances of Bach's church music were limited to some of his motets, and under [cantor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomaskantor "Thomaskantor") [Doles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Friedrich_Doles "Johann Friedrich Doles") some of his [Passions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Passions_(Bach) "Passions (Bach)").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitta1899b[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastianb02spituoftpage518mode2up_518–519],_[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastianb02spituoftpage611mode1up_611]_194-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitta1899b[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastianb02spituoftpage518mode2up_518%E2%80%93519],_[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastianb02spituoftpage611mode1up_611]-194">[192]</a></sup> A new generation of Bach aficionados emerged: they studiously collected and copied his music, including some of his large-scale works such as the [Mass in B minor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_in_B_minor "Mass in B minor") and performed it privately. One such connoisseur was [Gottfried van Swieten](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gottfried_van_Swieten "Gottfried van Swieten"), a high-ranking Austrian official who was instrumental in passing Bach's legacy on to the composers of the [Viennese school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Viennese_School "First Viennese School"). [Haydn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Haydn "Joseph Haydn") owned manuscript copies of _[The Well-Tempered Clavier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Well-Tempered_Clavier "The Well-Tempered Clavier")_ and the Mass in B minor and was influenced by Bach's music. [Mozart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart "Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart") owned a copy of one of Bach's motets,<sup id="cite_ref-195"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup> transcribed some of his instrumental works ([K. 404a](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=K._404a&action=edit&redlink=1 "K. 404a (page does not exist)"), [405](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=K._405&action=edit&redlink=1 "K. 405 (page does not exist)")),<sup id="cite_ref-196"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup> and wrote contrapuntal music influenced by his style.<sup id="cite_ref-198"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-apbrown_199-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-apbrown-199">[197]</a></sup> [Beethoven](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven "Ludwig van Beethoven") played the entire _Well-Tempered Clavier_ by the time he was 11 and described Bach as _Urvater der Harmonie_ (progenitor of harmony).<sup id="cite_ref-McKay_200-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-McKay-200">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schenk1959p101_201-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Schenk1959p101-201">[199]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-202">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKerst1904101_203-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKerst1904101-203">[201]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-204">[202]</a></sup>

### 19th century

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Altes_Bachdenkmal_%28Leipzig%29_-_Holzstich.jpg/170px-Altes_Bachdenkmal_%28Leipzig%29_-_Holzstich.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Altes_Bachdenkmal_(Leipzig)_-_Holzstich.jpg)

Image of the [Bach memorial](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=19th_century_Bach_memorial_(Leipzig)&action=edit&redlink=1 "19th century Bach memorial (Leipzig) (page does not exist)") \[[de](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altes_Bach-Denkmal_in_Leipzig "de:Altes Bach-Denkmal in Leipzig")\] erected by Felix Mendelssohn in Leipzig in 1843

In 1802, [Johann Nikolaus Forkel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Nikolaus_Forkel "Johann Nikolaus Forkel") published _[Johann Sebastian Bach: His Life, Art, and Work](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach:_His_Life,_Art,_and_Work "Johann Sebastian Bach: His Life, Art, and Work")_, the first Bach biography, dedicated to van Swieten.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeck20069–10_205-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeck20069%E2%80%9310-205">[203]</a></sup> In 1805, [Abraham Mendelssohn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Mendelssohn "Abraham Mendelssohn"), who had married one of Itzig's granddaughters, bought a substantial collection of Bach manuscripts that had come down from C. P. E. Bach, and donated it to the [Berlin Sing-Akademie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sing-Akademie_zu_Berlin "Sing-Akademie zu Berlin").<sup id="cite_ref-Wolff2005_192-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Wolff2005-192">[190]</a></sup> The Sing-Akademie occasionally performed Bach's works in public concerts, for instance his [first keyboard concerto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BWV_1052 "BWV 1052"), with Sara Itzig Levy at the piano.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolff2005_192-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Wolff2005-192">[190]</a></sup>

The first decades of the 19th century saw an increasing number of first publications of Bach's music: Breitkopf started publishing chorale preludes,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneider1907[httpsarchiveorgstreamBach-jahrbuch03jg1906BachJahrbuch1906pagen99mode1up_94]_206-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneider1907[httpsarchiveorgstreamBach-jahrbuch03jg1906BachJahrbuch1906pagen99mode1up_94]-206">[204]</a></sup> Hoffmeister harpsichord music,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneider1907[httpsarchiveorgstreamBach-jahrbuch03jg1906BachJahrbuch1906pagen101mode1up_96–97]_207-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneider1907[httpsarchiveorgstreamBach-jahrbuch03jg1906BachJahrbuch1906pagen101mode1up_96%E2%80%9397]-207">[205]</a></sup> and the _Well-Tempered Clavier_ was printed concurrently by Simrock (Germany), Nägeli (Switzerland) and Hoffmeister (Germany and Austria) in 1801.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchneider1907[httpsarchiveorgstreamBach-jahrbuch03jg1906BachJahrbuch1906pagen105mode1up_100]_208-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchneider1907[httpsarchiveorgstreamBach-jahrbuch03jg1906BachJahrbuch1906pagen105mode1up_100]-208">[206]</a></sup> Vocal music was also published: motets in 1802 and 1803, followed by the E♭ major version of the [Magnificat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magnificat_(Bach) "Magnificat (Bach)"), the [Kyrie-Gloria Mass in A major](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BWV_234 "BWV 234"), and the cantata [_Ein feste Burg ist unser Gott_ (BWV 80)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ein_feste_Burg_ist_unser_Gott,_BWV_80 "Ein feste Burg ist unser Gott, BWV 80").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen22mode1up_xvii]_209-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForkel1920[httpsarchiveorgstreamjohannsebastian01terrgoogpagen22mode1up_xvii]-209">[207]</a></sup> In 1818, [Hans Georg Nägeli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Georg_N%C3%A4geli "Hans Georg Nägeli") called the Mass in B minor the greatest composition ever.<sup id="cite_ref-McKay_200-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-McKay-200">[198]</a></sup> Bach's influence was felt in the next generation of early Romantic composers.<sup id="cite_ref-Schenk1959p101_201-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Schenk1959p101-201">[199]</a></sup> When Abraham's son Felix, aged 13, produced his first Magnificat setting in 1822, it is clear that he had been inspired by the then unpublished D major version of Bach's Magnificat.<sup id="cite_ref-210"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-210">[208]</a></sup>

[Felix Mendelssohn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felix_Mendelssohn "Felix Mendelssohn")'s 1829 performance of the _[St Matthew Passion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St_Matthew_Passion "St Matthew Passion")_ precipitated the Bach Revival. The _[St John Passion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St_John_Passion "St John Passion")_ saw its 19th-century premiere in 1833, and the first public performance of the Mass in B minor followed in 1844. Besides these and other public performances and an increased coverage on the composer and his compositions in printed media, the 1830s and 1840s also saw the first publication of more vocal works by Bach: six cantatas, the _St Matthew Passion_, and the Mass in B minor. A series of organ compositions saw their first publication in 1833.<sup id="cite_ref-211"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-211">[209]</a></sup> [Chopin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin "Frédéric Chopin") started composing his [24 Preludes, Op. 28](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/24_Preludes,_Op._28_(Chopin) "24 Preludes, Op. 28 (Chopin)"), inspired by the _Well-Tempered Clavier_, in 1835, and [Schumann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Schumann "Robert Schumann") published his _[Sechs Fugen über den Namen B-A-C-H](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Sechs_Fugen_%C3%BCber_den_Namen_B-A-C-H&action=edit&redlink=1 "Sechs Fugen über den Namen B-A-C-H (page does not exist)")_ in 1845. Bach's music was transcribed and arranged to suit contemporary tastes and performance practice by composers such as [Carl Friedrich Zelter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Zelter "Carl Friedrich Zelter"), [Robert Franz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Franz "Robert Franz"), and [Franz Liszt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franz_Liszt "Franz Liszt"), or combined with new music such as the melody line of [Charles Gounod](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Gounod "Charles Gounod")'s "[Ave Maria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ave_Maria_(Bach/Gounod) "Ave Maria (Bach/Gounod)")".<sup id="cite_ref-McKay_200-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-McKay-200">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKupferberg1985126_212-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKupferberg1985126-212">[210]</a></sup> [Brahms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johannes_Brahms "Johannes Brahms"), [Bruckner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anton_Bruckner "Anton Bruckner"), and [Wagner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_Wagner "Richard Wagner") were among the composers who promoted Bach's music or wrote glowingly about it.

In 1850, the _[Bach-Gesellschaft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach_Gesellschaft "Bach Gesellschaft")_ (Bach Society) was founded to promote Bach's music. In the second half of the 19th century, the Society published a comprehensive edition of the composer's works. In 1854, Bach was deemed one of the [three Bs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Three_Bs "Three Bs") by [Peter Cornelius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Cornelius "Peter Cornelius"), the other Bs being Beethoven and [Berlioz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlioz "Berlioz"). ([Hans von Bülow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_von_B%C3%BClow "Hans von Bülow") replaced Berlioz with Brahms.) From 1873 to 1880, [Philipp Spitta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philipp_Spitta "Philipp Spitta") published _[Johann Sebastian Bach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spitta%27s_Johann_Sebastian_Bach "Spitta's Johann Sebastian Bach")_, the standard work on Bach's life and music.<sup id="cite_ref-213"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-213">[211]</a></sup> Throughout the 19th century, 200 books were published on Bach. By the end of the century, local Bach societies were established in several cities, and his music had been performed in all major musical centres.<sup id="cite_ref-McKay_200-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-McKay-200">[198]</a></sup>

In Germany all throughout the century, Bach was coupled to nationalist feelings, and the composer was inscribed in a religious revival. In England, Bach was coupled to an existing revival of religious and baroque music. By the end of the century, Bach was firmly established as one of the greatest composers, recognised for both his instrumental and his vocal music.<sup id="cite_ref-McKay_200-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-McKay-200">[198]</a></sup>

### 20th century

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Statue_of_J.S._Bach_in_Leipzig.jpg/170px-Statue_of_J.S._Bach_in_Leipzig.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Statue_of_J.S._Bach_in_Leipzig.jpg)

1908 Statue of Bach in front of the Thomaskirche in Leipzig

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Fotothek_df_roe-neg_0002806_004_Besucher_der_Messe_in_der_Thomaskirche_zu_Ehren_Bachs.jpg/170px-Fotothek_df_roe-neg_0002806_004_Besucher_der_Messe_in_der_Thomaskirche_zu_Ehren_Bachs.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Fotothek_df_roe-neg_0002806_004_Besucher_der_Messe_in_der_Thomaskirche_zu_Ehren_Bachs.jpg)

28 July 1950: memorial service for Bach in Leipzig's Thomaskirche, on the 200th anniversary of the composer's death

During the 20th century, the process of recognising the musical as well as the [pedagogic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pedagogy "Pedagogy") value of some of the works continued, as in the promotion of the [cello suites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cello_Suites_(Bach) "Cello Suites (Bach)") by [Pablo Casals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pablo_Casals "Pablo Casals"), the first major performer to record these suites.<sup id="cite_ref-214"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-214">[212]</a></sup> Leading performers of classical music such as [Willem Mengelberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Willem_Mengelberg "Willem Mengelberg"), [Edwin Fischer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edwin_Fischer "Edwin Fischer"), [Georges Enescu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georges_Enescu "Georges Enescu"), [Herbert von Karajan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herbert_von_Karajan "Herbert von Karajan"), [Helmut Walcha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Helmut_Walcha "Helmut Walcha"), [Wanda Landowska](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wanda_Landowska "Wanda Landowska"), [I Musici](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I_Musici "I Musici"), [Dietrich Fischer-Dieskau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dietrich_Fischer-Dieskau "Dietrich Fischer-Dieskau"), and recorded his music.<sup id="cite_ref-215"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-215">[n 3]</a></sup>

A significant development in the later part of the 20th century was the [historically informed performance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historically_informed_performance "Historically informed performance") practice, with forerunners such as [Nikolaus Harnoncourt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikolaus_Harnoncourt "Nikolaus Harnoncourt") acquiring prominence by their performances of Bach's music. His keyboard music was again performed on the [harpsichord](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harpsichord "Harpsichord") and other Baroque instruments, rather than on modern pianos and 19th-century romantic organs. Ensembles playing and singing Bach's music not only kept to the instruments and the performance style of his day but were also reduced to the size of the groups Bach used for his performances.<sup id="cite_ref-216"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-216">[213]</a></sup> But that was far from the only way Bach's music came to the forefront in the 20th century: his music was heard in versions ranging from [Ferruccio Busoni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferruccio_Busoni "Ferruccio Busoni")'s late romantic [piano transcriptions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach-Busoni_Editions "Bach-Busoni Editions") to the orchestrations of [Leopold Stokowski](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leopold_Stokowski "Leopold Stokowski"), whose interpretation of the [Toccata and Fugue in D minor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toccata_and_Fugue_in_D_minor "Toccata and Fugue in D minor") opened [Walt Disney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walt_Disney "Walt Disney")'s [_Fantasia_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fantasia_(1940_film) "Fantasia (1940 film)"), to jazzy interpretations such as those by [The Swingle Singers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Swingle_Singers "The Swingle Singers") on their album _[Jazz Sebastian Bach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jazz_Sebastian_Bach "Jazz Sebastian Bach")_ and [electronic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_music "Electronic music") performances such as [Wendy Carlos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wendy_Carlos "Wendy Carlos")' _[Switched-On Bach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Switched-On_Bach "Switched-On Bach")_ and _[The Well-Tempered Synthesizer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Well-Tempered_Synthesizer "The Well-Tempered Synthesizer")_.

Bach's music has influenced other genres. [Jazz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jazz "Jazz") musicians have adopted Bach's music, with [Jacques Loussier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacques_Loussier "Jacques Loussier"), [Ian Anderson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ian_Anderson "Ian Anderson"), [Uri Caine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uri_Caine "Uri Caine"), and the [Modern Jazz Quartet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_Jazz_Quartet "Modern Jazz Quartet") among those creating jazz versions of his works.<sup id="cite_ref-217"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-217">[214]</a></sup> Several 20th-century composers referred to Bach or his music, for example [Eugène Ysaÿe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eug%C3%A8ne_Ysa%C3%BFe "Eugène Ysaÿe") in [Six Sonatas for solo violin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six_Sonatas_for_solo_violin_(Ysa%C3%BFe) "Six Sonatas for solo violin (Ysaÿe)"), [Dmitri Shostakovich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dmitri_Shostakovich "Dmitri Shostakovich") in [24 Preludes and Fugues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/24_Preludes_and_Fugues_(Shostakovich) "24 Preludes and Fugues (Shostakovich)") and [Heitor Villa-Lobos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heitor_Villa-Lobos "Heitor Villa-Lobos") in _[Bachianas Brasileiras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bachianas_Brasileiras "Bachianas Brasileiras")_. All kinds of publications involved Bach: not only were there the _Bach Jahrbuch_ publications of the Neue Bachgesellschaft, various other biographies and studies by among others [Albert Schweitzer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Schweitzer "Albert Schweitzer"), [Charles Sanford Terry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Sanford_Terry_(historian) "Charles Sanford Terry (historian)"), [Alfred Dürr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_D%C3%BCrr "Alfred Dürr"), [Christoph Wolff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christoph_Wolff "Christoph Wolff"). [Peter Williams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Williams_(musicologist) "Peter Williams (musicologist)"), [John Butt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Butt_(musician) "John Butt (musician)"),<sup id="cite_ref-218"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-218">[n 4]</a></sup> and the 1950 first edition of the [Bach-Werke-Verzeichnis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach-Werke-Verzeichnis "Bach-Werke-Verzeichnis"); but also books such as _[Gödel, Escher, Bach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G%C3%B6del,_Escher,_Bach "Gödel, Escher, Bach")_ put the composer's art in a wider perspective. Bach's music was extensively listened to, performed, broadcast, arranged, adapted, and commented upon in the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-KVNM2000_219-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-KVNM2000-219">[215]</a></sup> Around 2000, the 250th anniversary of Bach's death, three record companies issued box sets with complete recordings of Bach's music.<sup id="cite_ref-220"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-220">[216]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-221">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-222">[218]</a></sup>

Three works by Bach are featured on the [Voyager Golden Record](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voyager_Golden_Record "Voyager Golden Record"), a gramophone record containing a broad sample of the images, sounds, languages, and music of Earth, sent into space with the two [Voyager](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voyager_program "Voyager program") probes. The Bach pieces included are the First Movement of the [_Brandenburg Concerto_ No. 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brandenburg_Concertos "Brandenburg Concertos") (conducted by [Karl Richter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Richter_(conductor) "Karl Richter (conductor)")), the "Gavotte en rondeaux" from the [Partita for Violin No. 3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partita_for_Violin_No._3_(Bach) "Partita for Violin No. 3 (Bach)") (played by [Arthur Grumiaux](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Grumiaux "Arthur Grumiaux")) and the Prelude and Fugue in C, No. 1 from _The Well-Tempered Clavier_ (played by [Glenn Gould](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glenn_Gould "Glenn Gould")).<sup id="cite_ref-223"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-223">[219]</a></sup> Tributes to Bach in the 20th century include statues erected in his honour and a variety of things such as streets and space objects being named after him.<sup id="cite_ref-224"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-224">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-225">[221]</a></sup> Also, a multitude of musical ensembles such as the [Bach Aria Group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach_Aria_Group "Bach Aria Group"), [Deutsche Bachsolisten](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deutsche_Bachsolisten "Deutsche Bachsolisten"), [Bachchor Stuttgart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bachchor_Stuttgart "Bachchor Stuttgart"), and [Bach Collegium Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach_Collegium_Japan "Bach Collegium Japan") adopted the composer's name. [Bach festivals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach_festival "Bach festival") were held on several continents, and competitions and prizes such as the [International Johann Sebastian Bach Competition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Johann_Sebastian_Bach_Competition "International Johann Sebastian Bach Competition") and the [Royal Academy of Music Bach Prize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Academy_of_Music_Bach_Prize "Royal Academy of Music Bach Prize") were named after the composer. While by the end of the 19th century Bach had been inscribed in nationalism and religious revival, the late 20th century saw Bach as the subject of a secularised art-as-religion (_[Kunstreligion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kunstreligion "Kunstreligion")_).<sup id="cite_ref-McKay_200-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-McKay-200">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KVNM2000_219-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-KVNM2000-219">[215]</a></sup>

### 21st century

In the 21st century, Bach's compositions have become available online, for instance at the [International Music Score Library Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Music_Score_Library_Project "International Music Score Library Project").<sup id="cite_ref-226"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-226">[222]</a></sup> High-resolution facsimiles of Bach's autographs became available at the [Bach Digital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bach_Digital "Bach Digital") website.<sup id="cite_ref-227"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-227">[223]</a></sup> 21st-century biographers include [Christoph Wolff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christoph_Wolff "Christoph Wolff"), [Peter Williams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Williams_(musicologist) "Peter Williams (musicologist)") and [John Eliot Gardiner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Eliot_Gardiner "John Eliot Gardiner").<sup id="cite_ref-228"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-228">[n 5]</a></sup>

In 2015, Bach's handwritten personal copy of the Mass in B minor, held by the [Berlin State Library](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berlin_State_Library "Berlin State Library"), was added to [UNESCO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO")'s [Memory of the World Register](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Programme#Memory_of_the_World_Register "Memory of the World Programme"),<sup id="cite_ref-unesco_229-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-unesco-229">[224]</a></sup> a program intended to protect culturally significant manuscripts.

[Alex Ross](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alex_Ross_(music_critic) "Alex Ross (music critic)") writes: that "Bach became an absolute master of his art by never ceasing to be a student of it. His most exalted sacred works—the two extant Passions, from the seventeen-twenties, and the Mass in B Minor, completed not long before his death, in 1750—are feats of synthesis, mobilizing secular devices to spiritual ends. They are rooted in archaic chants, hymns, and chorales. They honor, with consummate skill, the scholastic discipline of canon and fugue. They make expert use of the word-painting techniques of the Renaissance madrigal and Baroque opera. They absorb such stock scenes as the lament, the pastoral, the lullaby, the rage aria, the tempest. They allude to courtly French dances, Italian love songs, the polonaise. Their furious development of brief motifs anticipates Beethoven, who worshipped Bach when he was young. And their most daring harmonic adventures—for example, the otherworldly modulations in the 'Confiteor' of the B-Minor Mass—look ahead to Wagner, even to Schoenberg."<sup id="cite_ref-230"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-230">[225]</a></sup>

In 2019, Bach was named the greatest composer of all time in a poll conducted among 174 living composers.<sup id="cite_ref-231"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-231">[226]</a></sup>

The [liturgical calendar of the Episcopal Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calendar_of_saints_(Episcopal_Church) "Calendar of saints (Episcopal Church)") remembers Bach annually with a [feast day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feast_day "Feast day") on 28 July;<sup id="cite_ref-232"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-232">[227]</a></sup> on the same day, the [Calendar of Saints](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calendar_of_saints_(Lutheran) "Calendar of saints (Lutheran)") of some [Lutheran churches](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lutheran_church "Lutheran church"), such as the [ELCA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_America "Evangelical Lutheran Church in America"), remembers Bach and Handel with [Heinrich Schütz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heinrich_Sch%C3%BCtz "Heinrich Schütz").<sup id="cite_ref-233"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-233">[228]</a></sup>

### Burial site

Bach was originally buried at Old St. John's Cemetery in Leipzig. His grave went unmarked for nearly 150 years, but in 1894 his remains were located and moved to a vault in St. John's Church. This building was destroyed by [Allied bombing during World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bombing_of_Leipzig_in_World_War_II "Bombing of Leipzig in World War II"), so in 1950 Bach's remains were taken to their present grave in St. Thomas Church.<sup id="cite_ref-Baroquenet_24-9"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-Baroquenet-24">[22]</a></sup> Later research has called into question whether the remains in the grave are actually those of Bach.<sup id="cite_ref-234"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#cite_note-234">[229]</a></sup>

## Further reading

_See: [Crist & Stauff 2011](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach#CITEREFCristStauff2011), for an extensive bibliography_.

-   Baron, Carol K. (2006). _Bach's Changing World: Voices in the Community_. Rochester, New York: [University of Rochester Press](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Rochester_Press "University of Rochester Press"). [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-1-58046-190-0](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-58046-190-0 "Special:BookSources/978-1-58046-190-0").
-   [Dörffel, Alfred](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alfred_D%C3%B6rffel "Alfred Dörffel") (1882). [_Thematisches Verzeichnis der Instrumentalwerke von Joh. Seb. Bach_](https://archive.org/details/thematischesverz00dr) (in German). Leipzig: [C. F. Peters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edition_Peters "Edition Peters"). _N.B_.: First published in 1867; superseded, for scholarly purposes, by [Wolfgang Schmieder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolfgang_Schmieder "Wolfgang Schmieder")'s complete thematic catalog, but useful as a handy reference tool for only the instrumental works of Bach and as a partial alternative to Schmieder's work.
